    concurrently for other sources of information; see [Appendix
    B](#mdnsmethods){.xref}.[¶](#section-4.1-3.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-4.1-3.2}

Once a proxy is discovered, the pledge communicates with a registrar
through the proxy using the bootstrapping protocol defined in [Section
5](#ProtocolDetails){.xref}.[¶](#section-4.1-4){.pilcrow}

While the GRASP M_FLOOD mechanism is passive for the pledge, the
non-normative other methods (mDNS and IPv4 methods) described in
[Appendix B](#mdnsmethods){.xref} are active. The pledge
[SHOULD]{.bcp14} run those methods in parallel with listening for the
M_FLOOD. The active methods [SHOULD]{.bcp14} back off by doubling to a
maximum of one hour to avoid overloading the network with discovery
attempts. Detection of physical link status change (Ethernet carrier,
for instance) [SHOULD]{.bcp14} reset the back-off
timers.[¶](#section-4.1-5){.pilcrow}

The pledge could discover more than one proxy on a given physical
interface. The pledge can have a multitude of physical interfaces as
well: a Layer 2/3 Ethernet switch may have hundreds of physical
ports.[¶](#section-4.1-6){.pilcrow}

Each possible proxy offer [SHOULD]{.bcp14} be attempted up to the point
where a valid voucher is received: while there are many ways in which
the attempt may fail, it does not succeed until the voucher has been
validated.[¶](#section-4.1-7){.pilcrow}

The connection attempts via a single proxy [SHOULD]{.bcp14}
exponentially back off to a maximum of one hour to avoid overloading the
network infrastructure. The back-off timer for each [MUST]{.bcp14} be
independent of other connection attempts.[¶](#section-4.1-8){.pilcrow}

Connection attempts [SHOULD]{.bcp14} be run in parallel to avoid
head-of-queue problems wherein an attacker running a fake proxy or
registrar could intentionally perform protocol actions slowly.
Connection attempts to different proxies [SHOULD]{.bcp14} be sent with
an interval of 3 to 5s. The pledge [SHOULD]{.bcp14} continue to listen
for additional GRASP M_FLOOD messages during the connection
attempts.[¶](#section-4.1-9){.pilcrow}

Each connection attempt through a distinct Join Proxy [MUST]{.bcp14}
have a unique nonce in the
voucher-request.[¶](#section-4.1-10){.pilcrow}

Once a connection to a registrar is established (e.g., establishment of
a TLS session key), there are expectations of more timely responses; see
[Section
5.2](#RequestVoucherFromRegistrar){.xref}.[¶](#section-4.1-11){.pilcrow}

Once all discovered services are attempted (assuming that none
succeeded), the device [MUST]{.bcp14} return to listening for GRASP
M_FLOOD. It [SHOULD]{.bcp14} periodically retry any
manufacturer-specific mechanisms. The pledge [MAY]{.bcp14} prioritize
selection order as appropriate for the anticipated
environment.[¶](#section-4.1-12){.pilcrow}

::: {#brskigrasp}
::: {#section-4.1.1 .section}
#### [4.1.1.](#section-4.1.1){.section-number .selfRef} [Proxy GRASP Announcements](#name-proxy-grasp-announcements){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-proxy-grasp-announcements}

A proxy uses the DULL GRASP M_FLOOD mechanism to announce itself. This
announcement can be within the same message as the ACP announcement
detailed in
\[[RFC8994](#RFC8994){.xref}\].[¶](#section-4.1.1-1){.pilcrow}

The formal Concise Data Definition Language (CDDL)
\[[RFC8610](#RFC8610){.xref}\] definition
is:[¶](#section-4.1.1-2){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-cddl-definition-of-proxy-di}

::: {#proxy_discovery_cddl}
::: {#section-4.1.1-3.1}
``` {.sourcecode .lang-CDDL}
<CODE BEGINS> file "proxygrasp.cddl"

flood-message = [M_FLOOD, session-id, initiator, ttl,
                 +[objective, (locator-option / [])]]

objective = ["AN_Proxy", objective-flags, loop-count,
                                       objective-value]

ttl             = 180000     ; 180,000 ms (3 minutes)
initiator = ACP address to contact registrar
objective-flags   = sync-only  ; as in the GRASP spec
sync-only         =  4         ; M_FLOOD only requires
                               ; synchronization
loop-count        =  1         ; one hop only
objective-value   =  any       ; none

locator-option    = [ O_IPv6_LOCATOR, ipv6-address,
                    transport-proto, port-number ]
ipv6-address      = the v6 LL of the Proxy
$transport-proto /= IPPROTO_TCP   ; note that this can be any value
                                 ; from the IANA protocol registry,
                                 ; as per RFC 8990, Section 2.9.5.1,
                                 ; Note 3.
port-number      = selected by Proxy

<CODE ENDS>
```
:::

[Figure 10](#figure-10){.selfRef}: [CDDL Definition of Proxy Discovery
Message](#name-cddl-definition-of-proxy-di){.selfRef}
:::

Here is an example M_FLOOD announcing a proxy at fe80::1, on TCP port
4443.[¶](#section-4.1.1-4){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-example-of-proxy-discovery-}

::: {#proxy_discovery_mflood}
::: {#section-4.1.1-5.1 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
    [M_FLOOD, 12340815, h'fe800000000000000000000000000001', 180000,
                [["AN_Proxy", 4, 1, ""],
                 [O_IPv6_LOCATOR,
                  h'fe800000000000000000000000000001', IPPROTO_TCP, 4443]]]
:::

[Figure 11](#figure-11){.selfRef}: [Example of Proxy Discovery
Message](#name-example-of-proxy-discovery-){.selfRef}
:::

On a small network, the registrar [MAY]{.bcp14} include the GRASP
M_FLOOD announcements to locally connected
networks.[¶](#section-4.1.1-6){.pilcrow}

The \$transport-proto above indicates the method that the
pledge-proxy-registrar will use. The TCP method described here is
mandatory, and other proxy methods, such as CoAP methods not defined in
this document, are optional. Other methods [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} be enabled
unless the Join Registrar ASA indicates support for them in its own
announcement.[¶](#section-4.1.1-7){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
:::
:::

::: {#coapconnection}
::: {#section-4.2 .section}
### [4.2.](#section-4.2){.section-number .selfRef} [CoAP Connection to Registrar](#name-coap-connection-to-registra){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-coap-connection-to-registra}

The use of CoAP to connect from pledge to registrar is out of scope for
this document and is described in future work. See
\[[ANIMA-CONSTRAINED-VOUCHER](#I-D.ietf-anima-constrained-voucher){.xref}\].[¶](#section-4.2-1){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#JRCgrasp}
::: {#section-4.3 .section}
### [4.3.](#section-4.3){.section-number .selfRef} [Proxy Discovery and Communication of Registrar](#name-proxy-discovery-and-communi){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-proxy-discovery-and-communi}

The registrar [SHOULD]{.bcp14} announce itself so that proxies can find
it and determine what kind of connections can be
terminated.[¶](#section-4.3-1){.pilcrow}

The registrar announces itself using GRASP M_FLOOD messages, with the
\"AN_join_registrar\" objective, within the ACP instance. A registrar
may announce any convenient port number, including use of stock port
443. ANI proxies [MUST]{.bcp14} support GRASP discovery of
registrars.[¶](#section-4.3-2){.pilcrow}

The M_FLOOD is formatted as follows:[¶](#section-4.3-3){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-an-example-of-a-registrar-a}

::: {#registrar_discovery_example1}
::: {#section-4.3-4.1 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
    [M_FLOOD, 51804321, h'fda379a6f6ee00000200000064000001', 180000,
                [["AN_join_registrar", 4, 255, "EST-TLS"],
                 [O_IPv6_LOCATOR,
                  h'fda379a6f6ee00000200000064000001', IPPROTO_TCP, 8443]]]
:::

[Figure 12](#figure-12){.selfRef}: [An Example of a Registrar
Announcement Message](#name-an-example-of-a-registrar-a){.selfRef}
:::

The formal CDDL definition is:[¶](#section-4.3-5){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-cddl-definition-for-registr}

::: {#registrar_discovery_cddl}
::: {#section-4.3-6.1}
``` {.sourcecode .lang-CDDL}
<CODE BEGINS> file "jrcgrasp.cddl"

flood-message = [M_FLOOD, session-id, initiator, ttl,
                 +[objective, (locator-option / [])]]

objective = ["AN_join_registrar", objective-flags, loop-count,
                                       objective-value]

initiator = ACP address to contact registrar
objective-flags = sync-only  ; as in the GRASP spec
sync-only =  4               ; M_FLOOD only requires
                             ; synchronization
loop-count      = 255        ; mandatory maximum
objective-value = text       ; name of the (list of) supported
                             ; protocols: "EST-TLS" for RFC 7030.

<CODE ENDS>
```
:::

[Figure 13](#figure-13){.selfRef}: [CDDL Definition for Registrar
Announcement Message](#name-cddl-definition-for-registr){.selfRef}
:::

The M_FLOOD message [MUST]{.bcp14} be sent periodically. The default
period [SHOULD]{.bcp14} be 60 seconds, and the value [SHOULD]{.bcp14} be
operator configurable but [SHOULD NOT]{.bcp14} be smaller than 60
seconds. The frequency of sending [MUST]{.bcp14} be such that the
aggregate amount of periodic M_FLOODs from all flooding sources causes
only negligible traffic across the ACP.[¶](#section-4.3-7){.pilcrow}

Here are some examples of locators for illustrative purposes. Only the
first one (\$transport-protocol = 6, TCP) is defined in this document
and is mandatory to implement.[¶](#section-4.3-8){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-4.3-9 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
    locator1  = [O_IPv6_LOCATOR, fd45:1345::6789, 6,  443]
    locator2  = [O_IPv6_LOCATOR, fd45:1345::6789, 17, 5683]
    locator3  = [O_IPv6_LOCATOR, fe80::1234, 41, nil]

[¶](#section-4.3-9){.pilcrow}
:::

A protocol of 6 indicates that TCP proxying on the indicated port is
desired.[¶](#section-4.3-10){.pilcrow}

Registrars [MUST]{.bcp14} announce the set of protocols that they
support, and they [MUST]{.bcp14} support TCP
traffic.[¶](#section-4.3-11){.pilcrow}

Registrars [MUST]{.bcp14} accept HTTPS/EST traffic on the TCP ports
indicated.[¶](#section-4.3-12){.pilcrow}

Registrars [MUST]{.bcp14} support the ANI TLS Circuit Proxy and
therefore BRSKI across HTTPS/TLS native across the
ACP.[¶](#section-4.3-13){.pilcrow}

In the ANI, the ACP-secured instance of GRASP
\[[RFC8990](#RFC8990){.xref}\] [MUST]{.bcp14} be used for discovery of
ANI registrar ACP addresses and ports by ANI proxies. Therefore, the TCP
leg of the proxy connection between the ANI proxy and ANI registrar also
runs across the ACP.[¶](#section-4.3-14){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
:::
:::

::: {#ProtocolDetails}
::: {#section-5 .section}
## [5.](#section-5){.section-number .selfRef} [Protocol Details (Pledge \-- Registrar \-- MASA)](#name-protocol-details-pledge-reg){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-protocol-details-pledge-reg}

The pledge [MUST]{.bcp14} initiate BRSKI after boot if it is
unconfigured. The pledge [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} automatically initiate BRSKI
if it has been configured or is in the process of being
configured.[¶](#section-5-1){.pilcrow}

BRSKI is described as extensions to EST \[[RFC7030](#RFC7030){.xref}\].
The goal of these extensions is to reduce the number of TLS connections
and crypto operations required on the pledge. The registrar implements
the BRSKI REST interface within the \"/.well-known/brski\" URI tree and
implements the existing EST URIs as described in EST
\[[RFC7030](#RFC7030){.xref}\], [Section
3.2.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7030#section-3.2.2){.relref}.
The communication channel between the pledge and the registrar is
referred to as \"BRSKI-EST\" (see [Figure
1](#architecturefigure){.xref}).[¶](#section-5-2){.pilcrow}

The communication channel between the registrar and MASA is a new
communication channel, similar to EST, within the newly registered
\"/.well-known/brski\" tree. For clarity, this channel is referred to as
\"BRSKI-MASA\" (see [Figure
1](#architecturefigure){.xref}).[¶](#section-5-3){.pilcrow}

The MASA URI is \"https://\" authority
\"/.well-known/brski\".[¶](#section-5-4){.pilcrow}

BRSKI uses existing CMS message formats for existing EST operations.
BRSKI uses JSON \[[RFC8259](#RFC8259){.xref}\] for all new operations
defined here and for voucher formats. In all places where a binary value
must be carried in a JSON string, a base64 format
(\[[RFC4648](#RFC4648){.xref}\], [Section
4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc4648#section-4){.relref}) is to be
used, as per \[[RFC7951](#RFC7951){.xref}\], [Section
6.6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7951#section-6.6){.relref}.[¶](#section-5-5){.pilcrow}

While EST (\[[RFC7030](#RFC7030){.xref}\], [Section
3.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7030#section-3.2){.relref}) does
not insist upon use of HTTP persistent connections
(\[[RFC7230](#RFC7230){.xref}\], [Section
6.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7230#section-6.3){.relref}),
BRSKI-EST connections [SHOULD]{.bcp14} use persistent connections. The
intention of this guidance is to ensure the provisional TLS state occurs
only once, and that the subsequent resolution of the provision state is
not subject to a Man-in-the-Middle (MITM) attack during a critical
phase.[¶](#section-5-6){.pilcrow}

If non-persistent connections are used, then both the pledge and the
registrar [MUST]{.bcp14} remember the certificates that have been seen
and also sent for the first connection. They [MUST]{.bcp14} check each
subsequent connection for the same certificates, and each end
[MUST]{.bcp14} use the same certificates as well. This places a
difficult restriction on rolling certificates on the
registrar.[¶](#section-5-7){.pilcrow}

Summarized automation extensions for the BRSKI-EST flow
are:[¶](#section-5-8){.pilcrow}

-   [The pledge either attempts concurrent connections via each
    discovered proxy or times out quickly and tries connections in
    series, as explained at the end of [Section
    5.1](#brskiesttls){.xref}.[¶](#section-5-9.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-5-9.1}
-   [The pledge provisionally accepts the registrar certificate during
    the TLS handshake as detailed in [Section
    5.1](#brskiesttls){.xref}.[¶](#section-5-9.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-5-9.2}
-   [The pledge requests a voucher using the new REST calls described
    below. This voucher is then
    validated.[¶](#section-5-9.3){.pilcrow}]{#section-5-9.3}
-   [The pledge completes authentication of the server certificate as
    detailed in [Section
    5.6.1](#CompletingAuthenticationBootstrapping){.xref}. This moves
    the BRSKI-EST TLS connection out of the provisional
    state.[¶](#section-5-9.4){.pilcrow}]{#section-5-9.4}
-   [Mandatory bootstrap steps conclude with voucher status telemetry
    (see [Section
    5.7](#pledgestatus){.xref}).[¶](#section-5-9.5){.pilcrow}]{#section-5-9.5}

The BRSKI-EST TLS connection can now be used for EST
enrollment.[¶](#section-5-10){.pilcrow}

The extensions for a registrar (equivalent to an EST server)
are:[¶](#section-5-11){.pilcrow}

-   [Client authentication is automated using IDevID as per the EST
    certificate-based client authentication. The subject field\'s DN
    encoding [MUST]{.bcp14} include the \"serialNumber\" attribute with
    the device\'s unique serial number as explained in [Section
    2.3.1](#PledgeIdentification){.xref}.[¶](#section-5-12.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-5-12.1}
-   [The registrar requests and validates the voucher from the
    MASA.[¶](#section-5-12.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-5-12.2}
-   [The registrar forwards the voucher to the pledge when
    requested.[¶](#section-5-12.3){.pilcrow}]{#section-5-12.3}
-   [The registrar performs log verifications (described in [Section
    5.8.3](#auditLogVerification){.xref}) in addition to local
    authorization checks before accepting optional pledge device
    enrollment requests.[¶](#section-5-12.4){.pilcrow}]{#section-5-12.4}

::: {#brskiesttls}
::: {#section-5.1 .section}
### [5.1.](#section-5.1){.section-number .selfRef} [BRSKI-EST TLS Establishment Details](#name-brski-est-tls-establishment){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-brski-est-tls-establishment}

The pledge establishes the TLS connection with the registrar through the
Circuit Proxy (see [Section 4](#proxydetails){.xref}), but the TLS
handshake is with the registrar. The BRSKI-EST pledge is the TLS client,
and the BRSKI-EST registrar is the TLS server. All security associations
established are between the pledge and the registrar regardless of proxy
operations.[¶](#section-5.1-1){.pilcrow}

Use of TLS 1.3 (or newer) is encouraged. TLS 1.2 or newer is
[REQUIRED]{.bcp14} on the pledge side. TLS 1.3 (or newer)
[SHOULD]{.bcp14} be available on the registrar server interface, and the
registrar client interface, but TLS 1.2 [MAY]{.bcp14} be used. TLS 1.3
(or newer) [SHOULD]{.bcp14} be available on the MASA server interface,
but TLS 1.2 [MAY]{.bcp14} be used.[¶](#section-5.1-2){.pilcrow}

Establishment of the BRSKI-EST TLS connection is as specified in
\"Bootstrap Distribution of CA Certificates\" (Section
[4.1.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7030#section-4.1.1){.relref})
of \[[RFC7030](#RFC7030){.xref}\], wherein the client is authenticated
with the IDevID certificate, and the EST server (the registrar) is
provisionally authenticated with an unverified server certificate.
Configuration or distribution of the trust anchor database used for
validating the IDevID certificate is out of scope of this specification.
Note that the trust anchors in / excluded from the database will affect
which manufacturers\' devices are acceptable to the registrar as pledges
and can also be used to limit the set of MASAs that are trusted for
enrollment.[¶](#section-5.1-3){.pilcrow}

The signature in the certificate [MUST]{.bcp14} be validated even if a
signing key cannot (yet) be validated. The certificate (or chain)
[MUST]{.bcp14} be retained for later
validation.[¶](#section-5.1-4){.pilcrow}

A self-signed certificate for the registrar is acceptable as the voucher
can validate it upon successful enrollment.[¶](#section-5.1-5){.pilcrow}

The pledge performs input validation of all data received until a
voucher is verified as specified in [Section
5.6.1](#CompletingAuthenticationBootstrapping){.xref} and the TLS
connection leaves the provisional state. Until these operations are
complete, the pledge could be communicating with an
attacker.[¶](#section-5.1-6){.pilcrow}

The pledge code needs to be written with the assumption that all data is
being transmitted at this point to an unauthenticated peer, and that
received data, while inside a TLS connection, [MUST]{.bcp14} be
considered untrusted. This particularly applies to HTTP headers and CMS
structures that make up the voucher.[¶](#section-5.1-7){.pilcrow}

A pledge that can connect to multiple registrars concurrently
[SHOULD]{.bcp14} do so. Some devices may be unable to do so for lack of
threading, or resource issues. Concurrent connections defeat attempts by
a malicious proxy from causing a TCP Slowloris-like attack (see
\[[slowloris](#slowloris){.xref}\]).[¶](#section-5.1-8){.pilcrow}

A pledge that cannot maintain as many connections as there are eligible
proxies will need to rotate among the various choices, terminating
connections that do not appear to be making progress. If no connection
is making progress after 5 seconds, then the pledge [SHOULD]{.bcp14}
drop the oldest connection and go on to a different proxy: the proxy
that has been communicated with least recently. If there were no other
proxies discovered, the pledge [MAY]{.bcp14} continue to wait, as long
as it is concurrently listening for new proxy
announcements.[¶](#section-5.1-9){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#RequestVoucherFromRegistrar}
::: {#section-5.2 .section}
### [5.2.](#section-5.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Pledge Requests Voucher from the Registrar](#name-pledge-requests-voucher-fro){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-pledge-requests-voucher-fro}

When the pledge bootstraps, it makes a request for a voucher from a
registrar.[¶](#section-5.2-1){.pilcrow}

This is done with an HTTPS POST using the operation path value of
\"/.well-known/brski/requestvoucher\".[¶](#section-5.2-2){.pilcrow}

The pledge voucher-request Content-Type is as
follows.[¶](#section-5.2-3){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

application/voucher-cms+json:
:   \[[RFC8366](#RFC8366){.xref}\] defines a \"YANG-defined JSON
    document that has been signed using a Cryptographic Message Syntax
    (CMS) structure\", and the voucher-request described in [Section
    3](#voucher-request){.xref} is created in the same way. The media
    type is the same as defined in \[[RFC8366](#RFC8366){.xref}\]. This
    is also used for the pledge voucher-request. The pledge
    [MUST]{.bcp14} sign the request using the credentials in [Section
    2.3](#IDevIDextension){.xref}.[¶](#section-5.2-4.2){.pilcrow}
:   

Registrar implementations [SHOULD]{.bcp14} anticipate future media types
but, of course, will simply fail the request if those types are not yet
known.[¶](#section-5.2-5){.pilcrow}

The pledge [SHOULD]{.bcp14} include an \"Accept\" header field (see
\[[RFC7231](#RFC7231){.xref}\], [Section
5.3.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7231#section-5.3.2){.relref})
indicating the acceptable media type for the voucher response. The
\"application/voucher-cms+json\" media type is defined in
\[[RFC8366](#RFC8366){.xref}\], but constrained voucher formats are
expected in the future. Registrars and MASA are expected to be flexible
in what they accept.[¶](#section-5.2-6){.pilcrow}

The pledge populates the voucher-request fields as
follows:[¶](#section-5.2-7){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

created-on:
:   Pledges that have a real-time clock are [RECOMMENDED]{.bcp14} to
    populate this field with the current date and time in
    yang:date-and-time format. This provides additional information to
    the MASA. Pledges that have no real-time clocks [MAY]{.bcp14} omit
    this field.[¶](#section-5.2-8.2){.pilcrow}
:   

nonce:
:   The pledge voucher-request [MUST]{.bcp14} contain a
    cryptographically strong random or pseudo-random number nonce (see
    \[[RFC4086](#RFC4086){.xref}\], [Section
    6.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc4086#section-6.2){.relref}).
    As the nonce is usually generated very early in the boot sequence,
    there is a concern that the same nonce might be generated across
    multiple boots, or after a factory reset. Different nonces
    [MUST]{.bcp14} be generated for each bootstrapping attempt, whether
    in series or concurrently. The freshness of this nonce mitigates
    against the lack of a real-time clock as explained in [Section
    2.6.1](#timeunknown){.xref}.[¶](#section-5.2-8.4){.pilcrow}
:   

assertion:
:   The pledge indicates support for the mechanism described in this
    document, by putting the value \"proximity\" in the voucher-request,
    and [MUST]{.bcp14} include the proximity-registrar-cert field
    (below).[¶](#section-5.2-8.6){.pilcrow}
:   

proximity-registrar-cert:
:   In a pledge voucher-request, this is the first certificate in the
    TLS server \"certificate_list\" sequence (see
    \[[RFC8446](#RFC8446){.xref}\], [Section
    4.4.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc8446#section-4.4.2){.relref})
    presented by the registrar to the pledge. That is, it is the
    end-entity certificate. This [MUST]{.bcp14} be populated in a pledge
    voucher-request.[¶](#section-5.2-8.8){.pilcrow}
:   

serial-number:
:   The serial number of the pledge is included in the voucher-request
    from the pledge. This value is included as a sanity check only, but
    it is not to be forwarded by the registrar as described in [Section
    5.5](#RequestVoucherFromMASA){.xref}.[¶](#section-5.2-8.10){.pilcrow}
:   

All other fields [MAY]{.bcp14} be omitted in the pledge
voucher-request.[¶](#section-5.2-9){.pilcrow}

See an example JSON payload of a pledge voucher-request in [Section
3.3](#voucher-request-examples){.xref}, Example
1.[¶](#section-5.2-10){.pilcrow}

The registrar confirms that the assertion is \"proximity\" and that
pinned proximity-registrar-cert is the registrar\'s certificate. If this
validation fails, then there is an on-path attacker (MITM), and the
connection [MUST]{.bcp14} be closed after the returning of an HTTP 401
error code.[¶](#section-5.2-11){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#pledgeauthorization}
::: {#section-5.3 .section}
### [5.3.](#section-5.3){.section-number .selfRef} [Registrar Authorization of Pledge](#name-registrar-authorization-of-){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-registrar-authorization-of-}

In a fully automated network, all devices must be securely identified
and authorized to join the domain.[¶](#section-5.3-1){.pilcrow}

A registrar accepts or declines a request to join the domain, based on
the authenticated identity presented. For different networks, examples
of automated acceptance may include the allowance
of:[¶](#section-5.3-2){.pilcrow}

-   [any device of a specific type (as determined by the X.509
    IDevID),[¶](#section-5.3-3.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-5.3-3.1}
-   [any device from a specific vendor (as determined by the X.509
    IDevID),[¶](#section-5.3-3.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-5.3-3.2}
-   [a specific device from a vendor (as determined by the X.509 IDevID)
    against a domain acceptlist. (The mechanism for checking a shared
    acceptlist potentially used by multiple registrars is out of
    scope.)[¶](#section-5.3-3.3){.pilcrow}]{#section-5.3-3.3}

If validation fails, the registrar [SHOULD]{.bcp14} respond with the
HTTP 404 error code. If the voucher-request is in an unknown format,
then an HTTP 406 error code is more appropriate. A situation that could
be resolved with administrative action (such as adding a vendor to an
acceptlist) [MAY]{.bcp14} be responded to with a 403 HTTP error
code.[¶](#section-5.3-4){.pilcrow}

If authorization is successful, the registrar obtains a voucher from the
MASA service (see [Section 5.5](#RequestVoucherFromMASA){.xref}) and
returns that MASA-signed voucher to the pledge as described in [Section
5.6](#VoucherResponse){.xref}.[¶](#section-5.3-5){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#brskimasatls}
::: {#section-5.4 .section}
### [5.4.](#section-5.4){.section-number .selfRef} [BRSKI-MASA TLS Establishment Details](#name-brski-masa-tls-establishmen){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-brski-masa-tls-establishmen}

The BRSKI-MASA TLS connection is a \"normal\" TLS connection appropriate
for HTTPS REST interfaces. The registrar initiates the connection and
uses the MASA URL that is obtained as described in [Section
2.8](#obtainmasaurl){.xref}. The mechanisms in
\[[RFC6125](#RFC6125){.xref}\] [SHOULD]{.bcp14} be used in
authentication of the MASA using a DNS-ID that matches that which is
found in the IDevID. Registrars [MAY]{.bcp14} include a mechanism to
override the MASA URL on a manufacturer-by-manufacturer basis, and
within that override, it is appropriate to provide alternate anchors.
This will typically be used by some vendors to establish explicit (or
private) trust anchors for validating their MASA that is part of a sales
channel integration.[¶](#section-5.4-1){.pilcrow}

Use of TLS 1.3 (or newer) is encouraged. TLS 1.2 or newer is
[REQUIRED]{.bcp14}. TLS 1.3 (or newer) [SHOULD]{.bcp14} be
available.[¶](#section-5.4-2){.pilcrow}

As described in \[[RFC7030](#RFC7030){.xref}\], the MASA and the
registrars [SHOULD]{.bcp14} be prepared to support TLS Client
Certificate authentication and/or HTTP Basic, Digest, or Salted
Challenge Response Authentication Mechanism (SCRAM) authentication. This
connection [MAY]{.bcp14} also have no client authentication at
all.[¶](#section-5.4-3){.pilcrow}

Registrars [SHOULD]{.bcp14} permit trust anchors to be preconfigured on
a per-vendor (MASA) basis. Registrars [SHOULD]{.bcp14} include the
ability to configure a TLS Client Certificate on a per-MASA basis, or to
use no Client Certificate. Registrars [SHOULD]{.bcp14} also permit HTTP
Basic and Digest authentication to be
configured.[¶](#section-5.4-4){.pilcrow}

The authentication of the BRSKI-MASA connection does not change the
voucher-request process, as voucher-requests are already signed by the
registrar. Instead, this authentication provides access control to the
audit-log as described in [Section
5.8](#authzLogRequest){.xref}.[¶](#section-5.4-5){.pilcrow}

Implementers are advised that contacting the MASA establishes a secured
API connection with a web service, and that there are a number of
authentication models being explored within the industry. Registrars are
[RECOMMENDED]{.bcp14} to fail gracefully and generate useful
administrative notifications or logs in the advent of unexpected HTTP
401 (Unauthorized) responses from the MASA.[¶](#section-5.4-6){.pilcrow}

::: {#masaauthentication}
::: {#section-5.4.1 .section}
#### [5.4.1.](#section-5.4.1){.section-number .selfRef} [MASA Authentication of Customer Registrar](#name-masa-authentication-of-cust){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-masa-authentication-of-cust}

Providing per-customer options requires the customer\'s registrar to be
uniquely identified. This can be done by any stateless method that HTTPS
supports such as HTTP Basic or Digest authentication (that is using a
password), but the use of TLS Client Certificate authentication is
[RECOMMENDED]{.bcp14}.[¶](#section-5.4.1-1){.pilcrow}

Stateful methods involving API tokens, or HTTP Cookies, are not
recommended.[¶](#section-5.4.1-2){.pilcrow}

It is expected that the setup and configuration of per-customer Client
Certificates is done as part of a sales ordering
process.[¶](#section-5.4.1-3){.pilcrow}

The use of public PKI (i.e., WebPKI) end-entity certificates to identify
the registrar is reasonable, and if done universally, this would permit
a MASA to identify a customer\'s registrar simply by a Fully Qualified
Domain Name (FQDN).[¶](#section-5.4.1-4){.pilcrow}

The use of DANE records in DNSSEC-signed zones would also permit use of
a FQDN to identify customer registrars.[¶](#section-5.4.1-5){.pilcrow}

A third (and simplest, but least flexible) mechanism would be for the
MASA to simply store the registrar\'s certificate pinned in a
database.[¶](#section-5.4.1-6){.pilcrow}

A MASA without any supply-chain integration can simply accept registrars
without any authentication or on a blind TOFU basis as described in
[Section
7.4.2](#masasecurityreduction_tofu){.xref}.[¶](#section-5.4.1-7){.pilcrow}

This document does not make a specific recommendation on how the MASA
authenticates the registrar as there are likely different tradeoffs in
different environments and product values. Even within the ANIMA ACP
applicability, there is a significant difference between supply-chain
logistics for \$100 CPE devices and \$100,000 core
routers.[¶](#section-5.4.1-8){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
:::
:::

::: {#RequestVoucherFromMASA}
::: {#section-5.5 .section}
### [5.5.](#section-5.5){.section-number .selfRef} [Registrar Requests Voucher from MASA](#name-registrar-requests-voucher-){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-registrar-requests-voucher-}

When a registrar receives a pledge voucher-request, it in turn submits a
registrar voucher-request to the MASA service via an HTTPS interface
\[[RFC7231](#RFC7231){.xref}\].[¶](#section-5.5-1){.pilcrow}

This is done with an HTTP POST using the operation path value of
\"/.well-known/brski/requestvoucher\".[¶](#section-5.5-2){.pilcrow}

The voucher media type \"application/voucher-cms+json\" is defined in
\[[RFC8366](#RFC8366){.xref}\] and is also used for the registrar
voucher-request. It is a JSON document that has been signed using a CMS
structure. The registrar [MUST]{.bcp14} sign the registrar
voucher-request.[¶](#section-5.5-3){.pilcrow}

MASA implementations [SHOULD]{.bcp14} anticipate future media ntypes
but, of course, will simply fail the request if those types are not yet
known.[¶](#section-5.5-4){.pilcrow}

The voucher-request CMS object includes some number of certificates that
are input to the MASA as it populates the pinned-domain-cert. As
\[[RFC8366](#RFC8366){.xref}\] is quite flexible in what may be put into
the pinned-domain-cert, the MASA needs some signal as to what
certificate would be effective to populate the field with: it may range
from the end-entity certificate that the registrar uses to the entire
private Enterprise CA certificate. More-specific certificates result in
a tighter binding of the voucher to the domain, while less-specific
certificates result in more flexibility in how the domain is represented
by certificates.[¶](#section-5.5-5){.pilcrow}

A registrar that is seeking a nonceless voucher for later offline use
benefits from a less-specific certificate, as it permits the actual key
pair used by a future registrar to be determined by the pinned
CA.[¶](#section-5.5-6){.pilcrow}

In some cases, a less-specific certificate, such as a public WebPKI CA,
could be too open and could permit any entity issued a certificate by
that authority to assume ownership of a device that has a voucher
pinned. Future work may provide a solution to pin both a certificate and
a name that would reduce such risk of malicious ownership
assertions.[¶](#section-5.5-7){.pilcrow}

The registrar [SHOULD]{.bcp14} request a voucher with the most
specificity consistent with the mode that it is operating in. In order
to do this, when the registrar prepares the CMS structure for the signed
voucher-request, it [SHOULD]{.bcp14} include only certificates that are
a part of the chain that it wishes the MASA to pin. This [MAY]{.bcp14}
be as small as only the end-entity certificate (with id-kp-cmcRA set)
that it uses as its TLS server certificate, or it [MAY]{.bcp14} be the
entire chain, including the domain CA.[¶](#section-5.5-8){.pilcrow}

The registrar [SHOULD]{.bcp14} include an \"Accept\" header field (see
\[[RFC7231](#RFC7231){.xref}\], [Section
5.3.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7231#section-5.3.2){.relref})
indicating the response media types that are acceptable. This list
[SHOULD]{.bcp14} be the entire list presented to the registrar in the
pledge\'s original request (see [Section
5.2](#RequestVoucherFromRegistrar){.xref}), but it [MAY]{.bcp14} be a
subset. The MASA is expected to be flexible in what it
accepts.[¶](#section-5.5-9){.pilcrow}

The registrar populates the voucher-request fields as
follows:[¶](#section-5.5-10){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

created-on:
:   The registrar [SHOULD]{.bcp14} populate this field with the current
    date and time when the voucher-request is formed. This field
    provides additional information to the
    MASA.[¶](#section-5.5-11.2){.pilcrow}
:   

nonce:
:   This value, if present, is copied from the pledge voucher-request.
    The registrar voucher-request [MAY]{.bcp14} omit the nonce as per
    [Section
    3.1](#noncelessVoucherRequest){.xref}.[¶](#section-5.5-11.4){.pilcrow}
:   

serial-number:
:   The serial number of the pledge the registrar would like a voucher
    for. The registrar determines this value by parsing the
    authenticated pledge IDevID certificate; see [Section
    2.3](#IDevIDextension){.xref}. The registrar [MUST]{.bcp14} verify
    that the serial-number field it parsed matches the serial-number
    field the pledge provided in its voucher-request. This provides a
    sanity check useful for detecting error conditions and logging. The
    registrar [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} simply copy the serial-number field
    from a pledge voucher-request as that field is claimed but not
    certified.[¶](#section-5.5-11.6){.pilcrow}
:   

idevid-issuer:
:   The Issuer value from the pledge IDevID certificate is included to
    ensure unique interpretation of the serial-number. In the case of a
    nonceless (offline) voucher-request, an appropriate value needs to
    be configured from the same out-of-band source as the
    serial-number.[¶](#section-5.5-11.8){.pilcrow}
:   

prior-signed-voucher-request:
:   The signed pledge voucher-request [SHOULD]{.bcp14} be included in
    the registrar voucher-request. The entire CMS-signed structure is to
    be included and base64 encoded for transport in the JSON
    structure.[¶](#section-5.5-11.10){.pilcrow}
:   

A nonceless registrar voucher-request [MAY]{.bcp14} be submitted to the
MASA. Doing so allows the registrar to request a voucher when the pledge
is offline, or when the registrar anticipates not being able to connect
to the MASA while the pledge is being deployed. Some use cases require
the registrar to learn the appropriate IDevID serialNumber field and
appropriate \"Accept\" header field values from the physical device
labeling or from the sales channel (which is out of scope for this
document).[¶](#section-5.5-12){.pilcrow}

All other fields [MAY]{.bcp14} be omitted in the registrar
voucher-request.[¶](#section-5.5-13){.pilcrow}

The proximity-registrar-cert field [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} be present in the
registrar voucher-request.[¶](#section-5.5-14){.pilcrow}

See example JSON payloads of registrar voucher-requests in [Section
3.3](#voucher-request-examples){.xref}, Examples 2 through
4.[¶](#section-5.5-15){.pilcrow}

The MASA verifies that the registrar voucher-request is internally
consistent but does not necessarily authenticate the registrar
certificate since the registrar [MAY]{.bcp14} be unknown to the MASA in
advance. The MASA performs the actions and validation checks described
in the following subsections before issuing a
voucher.[¶](#section-5.5-16){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-5.5.1 .section}
#### [5.5.1.](#section-5.5.1){.section-number .selfRef} [MASA Renewal of Expired Vouchers](#name-masa-renewal-of-expired-vou){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-masa-renewal-of-expired-vou}

As described in \[[RFC8366](#RFC8366){.xref}\], vouchers are normally
short lived to avoid revocation issues. If the request is for a previous
(expired) voucher using the same registrar (that is, a registrar with
the same domain CA), then the request for a renewed voucher
[SHOULD]{.bcp14} be automatically authorized. The MASA has sufficient
information to determine this by examining the request, the registrar
authentication, and the existing audit-log. The issuance of a renewed
voucher is logged as detailed in [Section
5.6](#VoucherResponse){.xref}.[¶](#section-5.5.1-1){.pilcrow}

To inform the MASA that existing vouchers are not to be renewed, one can
update or revoke the registrar credentials used to authorize the request
(see Sections [5.5.4](#MASAauthenticationOfRegistrar){.xref} and
[5.5.3](#revocationcheck){.xref}). More flexible methods will likely
involve sales channel integration and authorizations (details are out of
scope of this document).[¶](#section-5.5.1-2){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#MASApinned}
::: {#section-5.5.2 .section}
#### [5.5.2.](#section-5.5.2){.section-number .selfRef} [MASA Pinning of Registrar](#name-masa-pinning-of-registrar){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-masa-pinning-of-registrar}

A certificate chain is extracted from the registrar\'s signed CMS
container. This chain may be as short as a single end-entity
certificate, up to the entire registrar certificate chain, including the
domain CA certificate, as specified in [Section
5.5](#RequestVoucherFromMASA){.xref}.[¶](#section-5.5.2-1){.pilcrow}

If the domain\'s CA is unknown to the MASA, then it is considered a
temporary trust anchor for the rest of the steps in this section. The
intention is not to authenticate the message as having come from a fully
validated origin but to establish the consistency of the domain
PKI.[¶](#section-5.5.2-2){.pilcrow}

The MASA [MAY]{.bcp14} use the certificate in the chain that is farthest
from the end-entity certificate of the registrar, as determined by MASA
policy. A MASA [MAY]{.bcp14} have a local policy in which it only pins
the end-entity certificate. This is consistent with
\[[RFC8366](#RFC8366){.xref}\]. Details of the policy will typically
depend upon the degree of supply-chain integration and the mechanism
used by the registrar to authenticate. Such a policy would also
determine how the MASA will respond to a request for a nonceless
voucher.[¶](#section-5.5.2-3){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#revocationcheck}
::: {#section-5.5.3 .section}
#### [5.5.3.](#section-5.5.3){.section-number .selfRef} [MASA Check of the Voucher-Request Signature](#name-masa-check-of-the-voucher-r){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-masa-check-of-the-voucher-r}

As described in [Section 5.5.2](#MASApinned){.xref}, the MASA has
extracted the registrar\'s domain CA. This is used to validate the CMS
signature \[[RFC5652](#RFC5652){.xref}\] on the
voucher-request.[¶](#section-5.5.3-1){.pilcrow}

Normal PKIX revocation checking is assumed during voucher-request
signature validation. This CA certificate [MAY]{.bcp14} have Certificate
Revocation List (CRL) distribution points or Online Certificate Status
Protocol (OCSP) information \[[RFC6960](#RFC6960){.xref}\]. If they are
present, the MASA [MUST]{.bcp14} be able to reach the relevant servers
belonging to the registrar\'s domain CA to perform the revocation
checks.[¶](#section-5.5.3-2){.pilcrow}

The use of OCSP Stapling is preferred.[¶](#section-5.5.3-3){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#MASAauthenticationOfRegistrar}
::: {#section-5.5.4 .section}
#### [5.5.4.](#section-5.5.4){.section-number .selfRef} [MASA Verification of the Domain Registrar](#name-masa-verification-of-the-do){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-masa-verification-of-the-do}

The MASA [MUST]{.bcp14} verify that the registrar voucher-request is
signed by a registrar. This is confirmed by verifying that the
id-kp-cmcRA extended key usage extension field (as detailed in EST
\[[RFC7030](#RFC7030){.xref}\], [Section
3.6.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7030#section-3.6.1){.relref})
exists in the certificate of the entity that signed the registrar
voucher-request. This verification is only a consistency check to ensure
that the unauthenticated domain CA intended the voucher-request signer
to be a registrar. Performing this check provides value to the domain
PKI by assuring the domain administrator that the MASA service will only
respect claims from authorized registration authorities of the
domain.[¶](#section-5.5.4-1){.pilcrow}

Even when a domain CA is authenticated to the MASA, and there is strong
sales channel integration to understand who the legitimate owner is, the
above id-kp-cmcRA check prevents arbitrary end-entity certificates (such
as an LDevID certificate) from having vouchers issued against
them.[¶](#section-5.5.4-2){.pilcrow}

Other cases of inappropriate voucher issuance are detected by
examination of the audit-log.[¶](#section-5.5.4-3){.pilcrow}

If a nonceless voucher-request is submitted, the MASA [MUST]{.bcp14}
authenticate the registrar either as described in EST (see Sections
[3.2.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7030#section-3.2.3){.relref}
and
[3.3.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7030#section-3.3.2){.relref}
of \[[RFC7030](#RFC7030){.xref}\]) or by validating the registrar\'s
certificate used to sign the registrar voucher-request using a
configured trust anchor. Any of these methods reduce the risk of DDoS
attacks and provide an authenticated identity as an input to sales
channel integration and authorizations (details are out of scope of this
document).[¶](#section-5.5.4-4){.pilcrow}

In the nonced case, validation of the registrar\'s identity (via TLS
Client Certificate or HTTP authentication) [MAY]{.bcp14} be omitted if
the MASA knows that the device policy is to accept audit-only
vouchers.[¶](#section-5.5.4-5){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#MASAassertion}
::: {#section-5.5.5 .section}
#### [5.5.5.](#section-5.5.5){.section-number .selfRef} [MASA Verification of the Pledge \'prior-signed-voucher-request\'](#name-masa-verification-of-the-pl){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-masa-verification-of-the-pl}

The MASA [MAY]{.bcp14} verify that the registrar voucher-request
includes the prior-signed-voucher-request field. If so, the
prior-signed-voucher-request [MUST]{.bcp14} include a
proximity-registrar-cert that is consistent with the certificate used to
sign the registrar voucher-request. Additionally, the voucher-request
serial-number leaf [MUST]{.bcp14} match the pledge serial-number that
the MASA extracts from the signing certificate of the
prior-signed-voucher-request. The consistency check described above
entails checking that the proximity-registrar-cert Subject Public Key
Info (SPKI) Fingerprint exists within the registrar voucher-request CMS
signature\'s certificate chain. This is substantially the same as the
pin validation described in \[[RFC7469](#RFC7469){.xref}\], [Section
2.6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7469#section-2.6){.relref}.[¶](#section-5.5.5-1){.pilcrow}

If these checks succeed, the MASA updates the voucher and audit-log
assertion leafs with the \"proximity\" assertion, as defined by
\[[RFC8366](#RFC8366){.xref}\], [Section
5.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc8366#section-5.3){.relref}.[¶](#section-5.5.5-2){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#MASAnoncehandling}
::: {#section-5.5.6 .section}
#### [5.5.6.](#section-5.5.6){.section-number .selfRef} [MASA Nonce Handling](#name-masa-nonce-handling){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-masa-nonce-handling}

The MASA does not verify the nonce itself. If the registrar
voucher-request contains a nonce, and the prior-signed-voucher-request
exists, then the MASA [MUST]{.bcp14} verify that the nonce is
consistent. (Recall from above that the voucher-request might not
contain a nonce; see Sections [5.5](#RequestVoucherFromMASA){.xref} and
[5.5.4](#MASAauthenticationOfRegistrar){.xref}.)[¶](#section-5.5.6-1){.pilcrow}

The MASA populates the audit-log with the nonce that was verified. If a
nonceless voucher is issued, then the audit-log is to be populated with
the JSON value \"null\".[¶](#section-5.5.6-2){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
:::
:::

::: {#VoucherResponse}
::: {#section-5.6 .section}
### [5.6.](#section-5.6){.section-number .selfRef} [MASA and Registrar Voucher Response](#name-masa-and-registrar-voucher-){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-masa-and-registrar-voucher-}

The MASA voucher response to the registrar is forwarded without changes
to the pledge; therefore, this section applies to both the MASA and the
registrar. The HTTP signaling described applies to both the MASA and
registrar responses.[¶](#section-5.6-1){.pilcrow}

When a voucher-request arrives at the registrar, if it has a cached
response from the MASA for the corresponding registrar voucher-request,
that cached response can be used according to local policy; otherwise,
the registrar constructs a new registrar voucher-request and sends it to
the MASA.[¶](#section-5.6-2){.pilcrow}

Registrar evaluation of the voucher itself is purely for transparency
and audit purposes to further inform log verification (see [Section
5.8.3](#auditLogVerification){.xref}); therefore, a registrar could
accept future voucher formats that are opaque to the
registrar.[¶](#section-5.6-3){.pilcrow}

If the voucher-request is successful, the server (a MASA responding to a
registrar or a registrar responding to a pledge) response [MUST]{.bcp14}
contain an HTTP 200 response code. The server [MUST]{.bcp14} answer with
a suitable 4xx or 5xx HTTP \[[RFC7230](#RFC7230){.xref}\] error code
when a problem occurs. In this case, the response data from the MASA
[MUST]{.bcp14} be a plain text human-readable (UTF-8) error message
containing explanatory information describing why the request was
rejected.[¶](#section-5.6-4){.pilcrow}

The registrar [MAY]{.bcp14} respond with an HTTP 202 (\"the request has
been accepted for processing, but the processing has not been
completed\") as described in EST \[[RFC7030](#RFC7030){.xref}\],
[Section
4.2.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7030#section-4.2.3){.relref},
wherein the client \"[MUST]{.bcp14} wait at least the specified
\"retry-after\" time before repeating the same request\" (also see
\[[RFC7231](#RFC7231){.xref}\], [Section
6.6.4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7231#section-6.6.4){.relref}).
The pledge is [RECOMMENDED]{.bcp14} to provide local feedback (blinked
LED, etc.) during this wait cycle if mechanisms for this are available.
To prevent an attacker registrar from significantly delaying
bootstrapping, the pledge [MUST]{.bcp14} limit the Retry-After time to
60 seconds. Ideally, the pledge would keep track of the appropriate
Retry-After header field values for any number of outstanding
registrars, but this would involve a state table on the pledge. Instead,
the pledge [MAY]{.bcp14} ignore the exact Retry-After value in favor of
a single hard-coded value (a registrar that is unable to complete the
transaction after the first 60 seconds has another chance a minute
later). A pledge [SHOULD]{.bcp14} be willing to maintain a 202
retry-state for up to 4 days, which is longer than a long weekend, after
which time the enrollment attempt fails, and the pledge returns to
Discovery state. This allows time for an alert to get from the registrar
to a human operator who can make a decision as to whether or not to
proceed with the enrollment.[¶](#section-5.6-5){.pilcrow}

A pledge that retries a request after receiving a 202 message
[MUST]{.bcp14} resend the same voucher-request. It [MUST NOT]{.bcp14}
sign a new voucher-request each time, and in particular, it [MUST
NOT]{.bcp14} change the nonce value.[¶](#section-5.6-6){.pilcrow}

In order to avoid infinite redirect loops, which a malicious registrar
might do in order to keep the pledge from discovering the correct
registrar, the pledge [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} follow more than one
redirection (3xx code) to another web origin. EST supports redirection
but requires user input; this change allows the pledge to follow a
single redirection without a user
interaction.[¶](#section-5.6-7){.pilcrow}

A 403 (Forbidden) response is appropriate if the voucher-request is not
signed correctly or is stale or if the pledge has another outstanding
voucher that cannot be overridden.[¶](#section-5.6-8){.pilcrow}

A 404 (Not Found) response is appropriate when the request is for a
device that is not known to the MASA.[¶](#section-5.6-9){.pilcrow}

A 406 (Not Acceptable) response is appropriate if a voucher of the
desired type or that uses the desired algorithms (as indicated by the
\"Accept\" header fields and algorithms used in the signature) cannot be
issued as such because the MASA knows the pledge cannot process that
type. The registrar [SHOULD]{.bcp14} use this response if it determines
the pledge is unacceptable due to inventory control, MASA audit-logs, or
any other reason.[¶](#section-5.6-10){.pilcrow}

A 415 (Unsupported Media Type) response is appropriate for a request
that has a voucher-request or \"Accept\" value that is not
understood.[¶](#section-5.6-11){.pilcrow}

The voucher response format is as indicated in the submitted \"Accept\"
header fields or based on the MASA\'s prior understanding of proper
format for this pledge. Only the \"application/voucher-cms+json\" media
type \[[RFC8366](#RFC8366){.xref}\] is defined at this time. The
syntactic details of vouchers are described in detail in
\[[RFC8366](#RFC8366){.xref}\]. [Figure 14](#voucherjsonexample){.xref}
shows a sample of the contents of a
voucher.[¶](#section-5.6-12){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-an-example-voucher}

::: {#voucherjsonexample}
::: {#section-5.6-13.1}
``` {.sourcecode .lang-json}
{
  "ietf-voucher:voucher": {
    "nonce": "62a2e7693d82fcda2624de58fb6722e5",
    "assertion": "logged",
    "pinned-domain-cert": "base64encodedvalue==",
    "serial-number": "JADA123456789"
  }
}
```
:::

[Figure 14](#figure-14){.selfRef}: [An Example
Voucher](#name-an-example-voucher){.selfRef}
:::

The MASA populates the voucher fields as
follows:[¶](#section-5.6-14){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

nonce:
:   The nonce from the pledge if available. See [Section
    5.5.6](#MASAnoncehandling){.xref}.[¶](#section-5.6-15.2){.pilcrow}
:   

assertion:
:   The method used to verify the relationship between the pledge and
    registrar. See [Section
    5.5.5](#MASAassertion){.xref}.[¶](#section-5.6-15.4){.pilcrow}
:   

pinned-domain-cert:
:   A certificate; see [Section 5.5.2](#MASApinned){.xref}. This figure
    is illustrative; for an example, see [Appendix
    C.2](#exampleprocess){.xref} where an end-entity certificate is
    used.[¶](#section-5.6-15.6){.pilcrow}
:   

serial-number:
:   The serial-number as provided in the voucher-request. Also see
    [Section
    5.5.5](#MASAassertion){.xref}.[¶](#section-5.6-15.8){.pilcrow}
:   

domain-cert-revocation-checks:
:   Set as appropriate for the pledge\'s capabilities and as documented
    in \[[RFC8366](#RFC8366){.xref}\]. The MASA [MAY]{.bcp14} set this
    field to \"false\" since setting it to \"true\" would require that
    revocation information be available to the pledge, and this document
    does not make normative requirements for
    \[[RFC6961](#RFC6961){.xref}\], [Section
    4.4.2.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc8446#section-4.4.2.1){.relref}
    of \[[RFC8446](#RFC8446){.xref}\], or equivalent
    integrations.[¶](#section-5.6-15.10){.pilcrow}
:   

expires-on:
:   This is set for nonceless vouchers. The MASA ensures the voucher
    lifetime is consistent with any revocation or pinned-domain-cert
    consistency checks the pledge might perform. See [Section
    2.6.1](#timeunknown){.xref}. There are three times to consider: (a)
    a configured voucher lifetime in the MASA, (b) the expiry time for
    the registrar\'s certificate, and (c) any CRL lifetime. The
    expires-on field [SHOULD]{.bcp14} be before the earliest of these
    three values. Typically, (b) will be some significant time in the
    future, but (c) will typically be short (on the order of a week or
    less). The [RECOMMENDED]{.bcp14} period for (a) is on the order of
    20 minutes, so it will typically determine the life span of the
    resulting voucher. 20 minutes is sufficient time to reach the
    post-provisional state in the pledge, at which point there is an
    established trust relationship between the pledge and registrar. The
    subsequent operations can take as long as required from that point
    onwards. The lifetime of the voucher has no impact on the life span
    of the ownership relationship.[¶](#section-5.6-15.12){.pilcrow}
:   

Whenever a voucher is issued, the MASA [MUST]{.bcp14} update the
audit-log sufficiently to generate the response as described in [Section
5.8.1](#MASAauditlog){.xref}. The internal state requirements to
maintain the audit-log are out of scope.[¶](#section-5.6-16){.pilcrow}

::: {#CompletingAuthenticationBootstrapping}
::: {#section-5.6.1 .section}
#### [5.6.1.](#section-5.6.1){.section-number .selfRef} [Pledge Voucher Verification](#name-pledge-voucher-verification){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-pledge-voucher-verification}

The pledge [MUST]{.bcp14} verify the voucher signature using the
manufacturer-installed trust anchor(s) associated with the
manufacturer\'s MASA (this is likely included in the pledge\'s
firmware). Management of the manufacturer-installed trust anchor(s) is
out of scope of this document; this protocol does not update this trust
anchor(s).[¶](#section-5.6.1-1){.pilcrow}

The pledge [MUST]{.bcp14} verify that the serial-number field of the
signed voucher matches the pledge\'s own
serial-number.[¶](#section-5.6.1-2){.pilcrow}

The pledge [MUST]{.bcp14} verify the nonce information in the voucher.
If present, the nonce in the voucher must match the nonce the pledge
submitted to the registrar; vouchers with no nonce can also be accepted
(according to local policy; see [Section
7.2](#pledgeReductions){.xref}).[¶](#section-5.6.1-3){.pilcrow}

The pledge [MUST]{.bcp14} be prepared to parse and fail gracefully from
a voucher response that does not contain a pinned-domain-cert field.
Such a thing indicates a failure to enroll in this domain, and the
pledge [MUST]{.bcp14} attempt joining with other available Join
Proxies.[¶](#section-5.6.1-4){.pilcrow}

The pledge [MUST]{.bcp14} be prepared to ignore additional fields that
it does not recognize.[¶](#section-5.6.1-5){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#PledgeAuthenticationOfProvisionalTLS}
::: {#section-5.6.2 .section}
#### [5.6.2.](#section-5.6.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Pledge Authentication of Provisional TLS Connection](#name-pledge-authentication-of-pr){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-pledge-authentication-of-pr}

Following the process described in \[[RFC8366](#RFC8366){.xref}\], the
pledge should consider the public key from the pinned-domain-cert as the
sole temporary trust anchor.[¶](#section-5.6.2-1){.pilcrow}

The pledge then evaluates the TLS server certificate chain that it
received when the TLS connection was formed using this trust anchor. It
is possible that the public key in the pinned-domain-cert directly
matches the public key in the end-entity certificate provided by the TLS
server.[¶](#section-5.6.2-2){.pilcrow}

If a registrar\'s credentials cannot be verified using the
pinned-domain-cert trust anchor from the voucher, then the TLS
connection is discarded, and the pledge abandons attempts to bootstrap
with this discovered registrar. The pledge [SHOULD]{.bcp14} send voucher
status telemetry (described below) before closing the TLS connection.
The pledge [MUST]{.bcp14} attempt to enroll using any other proxies it
has found. It [SHOULD]{.bcp14} return to the same proxy again after
unsuccessful attempts with other proxies. Attempts should be made at
repeated intervals according to the back-off timer described earlier.
Attempts [SHOULD]{.bcp14} be repeated as failure may be the result of a
temporary inconsistency (an inconsistently rolled registrar key, or some
other misconfiguration). The inconsistency could also be the result of
an active MITM attack on the EST
connection.[¶](#section-5.6.2-3){.pilcrow}

The registrar [MUST]{.bcp14} use a certificate that chains to the
pinned-domain-cert as its TLS server
certificate.[¶](#section-5.6.2-4){.pilcrow}

The pledge\'s PKIX path validation of a registrar certificate\'s
validity period information is as described in [Section
2.6.1](#timeunknown){.xref}. Once the PKIX path validation is
successful, the TLS connection is no longer
provisional.[¶](#section-5.6.2-5){.pilcrow}

The pinned-domain-cert [MAY]{.bcp14} be installed as a trust anchor for
future operations such as enrollment (e.g., as recommended per
\[[RFC7030](#RFC7030){.xref}\]) or trust anchor management or raw
protocols that do not need full PKI-based key management. It can be used
to authenticate any dynamically discovered EST server that contains the
id-kp-cmcRA extended key usage extension as detailed in EST (see
\[[RFC7030](#RFC7030){.xref}\], [Section
3.6.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7030#section-3.6.1){.relref});
but to reduce system complexity, the pledge [SHOULD]{.bcp14} avoid
additional discovery operations. Instead, the pledge [SHOULD]{.bcp14}
communicate directly with the registrar as the EST server. The
pinned-domain-cert is not a complete distribution of the CA certificate
response, as described in \[[RFC7030](#RFC7030){.xref}\], [Section
4.1.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7030#section-4.1.3){.relref},
which is an additional justification for the recommendation to proceed
with EST key management operations. Once a full CA certificate response
is obtained, it is more authoritative for the domain than the limited
pinned-domain-cert response.[¶](#section-5.6.2-6){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
:::
:::

::: {#pledgestatus}
::: {#section-5.7 .section}
### [5.7.](#section-5.7){.section-number .selfRef} [Pledge BRSKI Status Telemetry](#name-pledge-brski-status-telemet){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-pledge-brski-status-telemet}

The domain is expected to provide indications to the system
administrators concerning device life-cycle status. To facilitate this,
it needs telemetry information concerning the device\'s
status.[¶](#section-5.7-1){.pilcrow}

The pledge [MUST]{.bcp14} indicate its pledge status regarding the
voucher. It does this by sending a status message to the
registrar.[¶](#section-5.7-2){.pilcrow}

The posted data media type:
application/json[¶](#section-5.7-3){.pilcrow}

The client sends an HTTP POST to the server at the URI
\".well-known/brski/voucher_status\".[¶](#section-5.7-4){.pilcrow}

The format and semantics described below are for version 1. A version
field is included to permit significant changes to this feedback in the
future. A registrar that receives a status message with a version larger
than it knows about [SHOULD]{.bcp14} log the contents and alert a
human.[¶](#section-5.7-5){.pilcrow}

The status field indicates if the voucher was acceptable. Boolean values
are acceptable, where \"true\" indicates the voucher was
acceptable.[¶](#section-5.7-6){.pilcrow}

If the voucher was not acceptable, the Reason string indicates why. In a
failure case, this message may be sent to an unauthenticated,
potentially malicious registrar; therefore, the Reason string [SHOULD
NOT]{.bcp14} provide information beneficial to an attacker. The
operational benefit of this telemetry information is balanced against
the operational costs of not recording that a voucher was ignored by a
client that the registrar expected was going to continue joining the
domain.[¶](#section-5.7-7){.pilcrow}

The reason-context attribute is an arbitrary JSON object (literal value
or hash of values) that provides additional information specific to this
pledge. The contents of this field are not subject to
standardization.[¶](#section-5.7-8){.pilcrow}

The version and status fields [MUST]{.bcp14} be present. The Reason
field [SHOULD]{.bcp14} be present whenever the status field is false.
The Reason-Context field is optional. In the case of a SUCCESS, the
Reason string [MAY]{.bcp14} be omitted.[¶](#section-5.7-9){.pilcrow}

The keys to this JSON object are case sensitive and [MUST]{.bcp14} be
lowercase. [Figure 16](#telemetryexample){.xref} shows an example
JSON.[¶](#section-5.7-10){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-cddl-for-voucher-status-pos}

::: {#cddl-voucherstatus}
::: {#section-5.7-11.1}
``` {.sourcecode .lang-CDDL}
<CODE BEGINS> file "voucherstatus.cddl"

voucherstatus-post = {
    "version": uint,
    "status": bool,
    ? "reason": text,
    ? "reason-context" : { $$arbitrary-map }
  }
}

<CODE ENDS>
```
:::

[Figure 15](#figure-15){.selfRef}: [CDDL for Voucher Status
POST](#name-cddl-for-voucher-status-pos){.selfRef}
:::

[]{#name-example-status-telemetry}

::: {#telemetryexample}
::: {#section-5.7-12.1}
``` {.sourcecode .lang-json}
{
    "version": 1,
    "status":false,
    "reason":"Informative human-readable message",
    "reason-context": { "additional" : "JSON" }
}
```
:::

[Figure 16](#figure-16){.selfRef}: [Example Status
Telemetry](#name-example-status-telemetry){.selfRef}
:::

The server [SHOULD]{.bcp14} respond with an HTTP 200 but [MAY]{.bcp14}
simply fail with an HTTP 404 error. The client ignores any response. The
server [SHOULD]{.bcp14} capture this telemetry information within the
server logs.[¶](#section-5.7-13){.pilcrow}

Additional standard JSON fields in this POST [MAY]{.bcp14} be added; see
[Section 8.5](#pledgestatustelemetryregistry){.xref}. A server that sees
unknown fields should log them, but otherwise ignore
them.[¶](#section-5.7-14){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#authzLogRequest}
::: {#section-5.8 .section}
### [5.8.](#section-5.8){.section-number .selfRef} [Registrar Audit-Log Request](#name-registrar-audit-log-request){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-registrar-audit-log-request}

After receiving the pledge status telemetry (see [Section
5.7](#pledgestatus){.xref}), the registrar [SHOULD]{.bcp14} request the
MASA audit-log from the MASA service.[¶](#section-5.8-1){.pilcrow}

This is done with an HTTP POST using the operation path value of
\"/.well-known/brski/requestauditlog\".[¶](#section-5.8-2){.pilcrow}

The registrar [SHOULD]{.bcp14} HTTP POST the same registrar
voucher-request as it did when requesting a voucher (using the same
Content-Type). It is posted to the /requestauditlog URI instead. The
idevid-issuer and serial-number informs the MASA which log is requested,
so the appropriate log can be prepared for the response. Using the same
media type and message minimizes cryptographic and message operations,
although it results in additional network traffic. The relying MASA
implementation [MAY]{.bcp14} leverage internal state to associate this
request with the original, and by now already validated, voucher-request
so as to avoid an extra crypto validation.[¶](#section-5.8-3){.pilcrow}

A registrar [MAY]{.bcp14} request logs at future times. If the registrar
generates a new request, then the MASA is forced to perform the
additional cryptographic operations to verify the new
request.[¶](#section-5.8-4){.pilcrow}

A MASA that receives a request for a device that does not exist, or for
which the requesting owner was never an owner, returns an HTTP 404
(\"Not found\") code.[¶](#section-5.8-5){.pilcrow}

It is reasonable for a registrar, that the MASA does not believe to be
the current owner, to request the audit-log. There are probably reasons
for this, which are hard to predict in advance. For instance, such a
registrar may not be aware that the device has been resold; it may be
that the device has been resold inappropriately, and this is how the
original owner will learn of the occurrence. It is also possible that
the device legitimately spends time in two different
networks.[¶](#section-5.8-6){.pilcrow}

Rather than returning the audit-log as a response to the POST (with a
return code 200), the MASA [MAY]{.bcp14} instead return a 201
(\"Created\") response (\[[RFC7231](#RFC7231){.xref}\], Sections
[6.3.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7231#section-6.3.2){.relref}
and [7.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7231#section-7.1){.relref}),
with the URL to the prepared (and idempotent, therefore cachable) audit
response in the \"Location\" header field.[¶](#section-5.8-7){.pilcrow}

In order to avoid enumeration of device audit-logs, a MASA that returns
URLs [SHOULD]{.bcp14} take care to make the returned URL unguessable.
\[[W3C.capability-urls](#W3C.capability-urls){.xref}\] provides very
good additional guidance. For instance, rather than returning URLs
containing a database number such as https://example.com/auditlog/1234
or the Extended Unique Identifier (EUI) of the device such
https://example.com/auditlog/10-00-00-11-22-33, the MASA
[SHOULD]{.bcp14} return a randomly generated value (a \"slug\" in web
parlance). The value is used to find the relevant database
entry.[¶](#section-5.8-8){.pilcrow}

A MASA that returns a code 200 [MAY]{.bcp14} also include a \"Location\"
header for future reference by the
registrar.[¶](#section-5.8-9){.pilcrow}

::: {#MASAauditlog}
::: {#section-5.8.1 .section}
#### [5.8.1.](#section-5.8.1){.section-number .selfRef} [MASA Audit-Log Response](#name-masa-audit-log-response){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-masa-audit-log-response}

A log data file is returned consisting of all log entries associated
with the device selected by the IDevID presented in the request. The
audit-log may be abridged by removal of old or repeated values as
explained below. The returned data is in JSON format
\[[RFC8259](#RFC8259){.xref}\], and the Content-Type [SHOULD]{.bcp14} be
\"application/json\".[¶](#section-5.8.1-1){.pilcrow}

The following CDDL \[[RFC8610](#RFC8610){.xref}\] explains the structure
of the JSON format audit-log response:[¶](#section-5.8.1-2){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-cddl-for-audit-log-response}

::: {#cddl-auditlog}
::: {#section-5.8.1-3.1}
``` {.sourcecode .lang-CDDL}
<CODE BEGINS> file "auditlog.cddl"

audit-log-response = {
  "version": uint,
  "events": [ + event ]
  "truncation": {
    ? "nonced duplicates": uint,
    ? "nonceless duplicates": uint,
    ? "arbitrary": uint,
  }
}

event = {
  "date": text,
  "domainID": text,
  "nonce": text / null,
  "assertion": "verified" / "logged" / "proximity",
  ? "truncated": uint,
}

<CODE ENDS>
```
:::

[Figure 17](#figure-17){.selfRef}: [CDDL for Audit-Log
Response](#name-cddl-for-audit-log-response){.selfRef}
:::

An example:[¶](#section-5.8.1-4){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-example-of-an-audit-log-res}

::: {#example-auditlog}
::: {#section-5.8.1-5.1}
``` {.sourcecode .lang-json}
{
  "version":"1",
  "events":[
    {
        "date":"2019-05-15T17:25:55.644-04:00",
        "domainID":"BduJhdHPpfhQLyponf48JzXSGZ8=",
        "nonce":"VOUFT-WwrEv0NuAQEHoV7Q",
        "assertion":"proximity",
        "truncated":"0"
    },
    {
        "date":"2017-05-15T17:25:55.644-04:00",
        "domainID":"BduJhdHPpfhQLyponf48JzXSGZ8=",
        "nonce":"f4G6Vi1t8nKo/FieCVgpBg==",
        "assertion":"proximity"
    }
  ],
    "truncation": {
        "nonced duplicates": "0",
        "nonceless duplicates": "1",
        "arbitrary": "2"
     }
}
```
:::

[Figure 18](#figure-18){.selfRef}: [Example of an Audit-Log
Response](#name-example-of-an-audit-log-res){.selfRef}
:::

The domainID is a binary SubjectKeyIdentifier value calculated according
to [Section 5.8.2](#domainID){.xref}. It is encoded once in base64 in
order to be transported in this JSON
container.[¶](#section-5.8.1-6){.pilcrow}

The date is formatted per \[[RFC3339](#RFC3339){.xref}\], which is
consistent with typical JavaScript usage of
JSON.[¶](#section-5.8.1-7){.pilcrow}

The truncation structure [MAY]{.bcp14} be omitted if all values are
zero. Any counter missing from the truncation structure is assumed to be
zero.[¶](#section-5.8.1-8){.pilcrow}

The nonce is a string, as provided in the voucher-request, and is used
in the voucher. If no nonce was placed in the resulting voucher, then a
value of null [SHOULD]{.bcp14} be used in preference to omitting the
entry. While the nonce is often created as a base64-encoded random
series of bytes, this should not be
assumed.[¶](#section-5.8.1-9){.pilcrow}

Distribution of a large log is less than ideal. This structure can be
optimized as follows: nonced or nonceless entries for the same domainID
[MAY]{.bcp14} be abridged from the log leaving only the single most
recent nonced or nonceless entry for that domainID. In the case of
truncation, the \"event\" truncation value [SHOULD]{.bcp14} contain a
count of the number of events for this domainID that were omitted. The
log [SHOULD NOT]{.bcp14} be further reduced, but an operational
situation could exist where maintaining the full log is not possible. In
such situations, the log [MAY]{.bcp14} be arbitrarily abridged for
length, with the number of removed entries indicated as
\"arbitrary\".[¶](#section-5.8.1-10){.pilcrow}

If the truncation count exceeds 1024, then the MASA [MAY]{.bcp14} use
this value without further incrementing
it.[¶](#section-5.8.1-11){.pilcrow}

A log where duplicate entries for the same domain have been omitted
(\"nonced duplicates\" and/or \"nonceless duplicates\") could still be
acceptable for informed decisions. A log that has had \"arbitrary\"
truncations is less acceptable, but manufacturer transparency is better
than hidden truncations.[¶](#section-5.8.1-12){.pilcrow}

A registrar that sees a version value greater than 1 indicates an
audit-log format that has been enhanced with additional information. No
information will be removed in future versions; should an incompatible
change be desired in the future, then a new HTTP endpoint will be
used.[¶](#section-5.8.1-13){.pilcrow}

This document specifies a simple log format as provided by the MASA
service to the registrar. This format could be improved by distributed
consensus technologies that integrate vouchers with technologies such as
block-chain or hash trees or optimized logging approaches. Doing so is
out of the scope of this document but is an anticipated improvement for
future work. As such, the registrar [SHOULD]{.bcp14} anticipate new
kinds of responses and [SHOULD]{.bcp14} provide operator controls to
indicate how to process unknown
responses.[¶](#section-5.8.1-14){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#domainID}
::: {#section-5.8.2 .section}
#### [5.8.2.](#section-5.8.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Calculation of domainID](#name-calculation-of-domainid){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-calculation-of-domainid}

The domainID is a binary value (a BIT STRING) that uniquely identifies a
registrar by the pinned-domain-cert.[¶](#section-5.8.2-1){.pilcrow}

If the pinned-domain-cert certificate includes the SubjectKeyIdentifier
(\[[RFC5280](#RFC5280){.xref}\], [Section
4.2.1.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5280#section-4.2.1.2){.relref}),
then it is used as the domainID. If not, the SPKI Fingerprint as
described in \[[RFC7469](#RFC7469){.xref}\], [Section
2.4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7469#section-2.4){.relref} is
used. This value needs to be calculated by both the MASA (to populate
the audit-log) and the registrar (to recognize itself in the
audit-log).[¶](#section-5.8.2-2){.pilcrow}

\[[RFC5280](#RFC5280){.xref}\], [Section
4.2.1.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5280#section-4.2.1.2){.relref}
does not mandate that the SubjectKeyIdentifier extension be present in
non-CA certificates. It is [RECOMMENDED]{.bcp14} that registrar
certificates (even if self-signed) always include the
SubjectKeyIdentifier to be used as a
domainID.[¶](#section-5.8.2-3){.pilcrow}

The domainID is determined from the certificate chain associated with
the pinned-domain-cert and is used to update the
audit-log.[¶](#section-5.8.2-4){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#auditLogVerification}
::: {#section-5.8.3 .section}
#### [5.8.3.](#section-5.8.3){.section-number .selfRef} [Registrar Audit-Log Verification](#name-registrar-audit-log-verific){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-registrar-audit-log-verific}

Each time the MASA issues a voucher, it appends details of the
assignment to an internal audit-log for that device. The internal
audit-log is processed when responding to requests for details as
described in [Section 5.8](#authzLogRequest){.xref}. The contents of the
audit-log can express a variety of trust levels, and this section
explains what kind of trust a registrar can derive from the
entries.[¶](#section-5.8.3-1){.pilcrow}

While the audit-log provides a list of vouchers that were issued by the
MASA, the vouchers are issued in response to voucher-requests, and it is
the content of the voucher-requests that determines how meaningful the
audit-log entries are.[¶](#section-5.8.3-2){.pilcrow}

A registrar [SHOULD]{.bcp14} use the log information to make an informed
decision regarding the continued bootstrapping of the pledge. The exact
policy is out of scope of this document as it depends on the security
requirements within the registrar domain. Equipment that is purchased
preowned can be expected to have an extensive history. The following
discussion is provided to help explain the value of each log
element:[¶](#section-5.8.3-3){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

date:
:   The date field provides the registrar an opportunity to divide the
    log around known events such as the purchase date. Depending on the
    context known to the registrar or administrator, events before/after
    certain dates can have different levels of importance. For example,
    for equipment that is expected to be new, and thus has no history,
    it would be a surprise to find prior
    entries.[¶](#section-5.8.3-4.2){.pilcrow}
:   

domainID:
:   If the log includes an unexpected domainID, then the pledge could
    have imprinted on an unexpected domain. The registrar can be
    expected to use a variety of techniques to define \"unexpected\"
    ranging from acceptlists of prior domains to anomaly detection
    (e.g., \"this device was previously bound to a different domain than
    any other device deployed\"). Log entries can also be compared
    against local history logs in search of discrepancies (e.g., \"this
    device was re-deployed some number of times internally, but the
    external audit-log shows additional re-deployments our internal logs
    are unaware of\").[¶](#section-5.8.3-4.4){.pilcrow}
:   

nonce:
:   Nonceless entries mean the logged domainID could theoretically
    trigger a reset of the pledge and then take over management by using
    the existing nonceless voucher.[¶](#section-5.8.3-4.6){.pilcrow}
:   

assertion:
:   The assertion leaf in the voucher and audit-log indicates why the
    MASA issued the voucher. A \"verified\" entry means that the MASA
    issued the associated voucher as a result of positive verification
    of ownership. However, this entry does not indicate whether or not
    the pledge was actually deployed in the prior domain. A \"logged\"
    assertion informs the registrar that the prior vouchers were issued
    with minimal verification. A \"proximity\" assertion assures the
    registrar that the pledge was truly communicating with the prior
    domain and thus provides assurance that the prior domain really has
    deployed the pledge.[¶](#section-5.8.3-4.8){.pilcrow}
:   

A relatively simple policy is to acceptlist known (internal or external)
domainIDs and require all vouchers to have a nonce. An alternative is to
require that all nonceless vouchers be from a subset (e.g., only
internal) of domainIDs. If the policy is violated, a simple action is to
revoke any locally issued credentials for the pledge in question or to
refuse to forward the voucher. The registrar [MUST]{.bcp14} then refuse
any EST actions and [SHOULD]{.bcp14} inform a human via a log. A
registrar [MAY]{.bcp14} be configured to ignore (i.e., override the
above policy) the history of the device, but it is [RECOMMENDED]{.bcp14}
that this only be configured if hardware-assisted (i.e., Transport
Performance Metrics (TPM) anchored) Network Endpoint Assessment (NEA)
\[[RFC5209](#RFC5209){.xref}\] is
supported.[¶](#section-5.8.3-5){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
:::
:::

::: {#ESTintegration}
::: {#section-5.9 .section}
### [5.9.](#section-5.9){.section-number .selfRef} [EST Integration for PKI Bootstrapping](#name-est-integration-for-pki-boo){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-est-integration-for-pki-boo}

The pledge [SHOULD]{.bcp14} follow the BRSKI operations with EST
enrollment operations including \"CA Certificates Request\", \"CSR
Attributes Request\", and \"Client Certificate Request\" or
\"Server-Side Key Generation\", etc. This is a relatively seamless
integration since BRSKI API calls provide an automated alternative to
the manual bootstrapping method described in
\[[RFC7030](#RFC7030){.xref}\]. As noted above, use of HTTP-persistent
connections simplifies the pledge state
machine.[¶](#section-5.9-1){.pilcrow}

Although EST allows clients to obtain multiple certificates by sending
multiple Certificate Signing Requests (CSRs), BRSKI does not support
this mechanism directly. This is because BRSKI pledges [MUST]{.bcp14}
use the CSR Attributes request (\[[RFC7030](#RFC7030){.xref}\], [Section
4.5](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7030#section-4.5){.relref}). The
registrar [MUST]{.bcp14} validate the CSR against the expected
attributes. This implies that client requests will \"look the same\" and
therefore result in a single logical certificate being issued even if
the client were to make multiple requests. Registrars [MAY]{.bcp14}
contain more complex logic, but doing so is out of scope of this
specification. BRSKI does not signal any enhancement or restriction to
this capability.[¶](#section-5.9-2){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-5.9.1 .section}
#### [5.9.1.](#section-5.9.1){.section-number .selfRef} [EST Distribution of CA Certificates](#name-est-distribution-of-ca-cert){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-est-distribution-of-ca-cert}

The pledge [SHOULD]{.bcp14} request the full EST Distribution of CA
certificate messages; see \[[RFC7030](#RFC7030){.xref}\], [Section
4.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7030#section-4.1){.relref}.[¶](#section-5.9.1-1){.pilcrow}

This ensures that the pledge has the complete set of current CA
certificates beyond the pinned-domain-cert (see [Section
5.6.2](#PledgeAuthenticationOfProvisionalTLS){.xref} for a discussion of
the limitations inherent in having a single certificate instead of a
full CA certificate response). Although these limitations are acceptable
during initial bootstrapping, they are not appropriate for ongoing PKIX
end-entity certificate validation.[¶](#section-5.9.1-2){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#csrattributes}
::: {#section-5.9.2 .section}
